However, our knowledge of how zinc affects corals is still limited. We tested the effects of zinc supplementation (0, 1, 10 and 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>) on health, growth, NDVI (a proxy for chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>) and overall colouration of the stony coral <jats:italic>Stylophora pistillata</jats:italic>. After two weeks, no signs of necrosis were observed in any of the treatments. However, at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>, we detected a considerable ~62% growth reduction compared to zinc levels of 0 to 10 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>. In addition, NDVI was significantly reduced by ~36% at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup> zinc, indicating loss of chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>. Zinc did not affect coral colouration in general, although reflection intensity increased markedly at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>, most likely due to a loss of chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>. In conclusion, the No Observed Effect Concentration (NOEC) after a two\u2013week zinc exposure was 10 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup> for <jats:italic>S. pistillata</jats:italic>. "content-version": "unspecified"}], "content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "abstract": "<jats:p>Zinc levels in artificial seawater are often unnaturally elevated, and thus potentially toxic to aquacultured corals. However, our knowledge of how zinc affects corals is still limited. We tested the effects of zinc supplementation (0, 1, 10 and 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>) on health, growth, NDVI (a proxy for chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>) and overall colouration of the stony coral <jats:italic>Stylophora pistillata</jats:italic>. After two weeks, no signs of necrosis were observed in any of the treatments. However, at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>, we detected a considerable ~62% growth reduction compared to zinc levels of 0 to 10 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>. In addition, NDVI was significantly reduced by ~36% at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup> zinc, indicating loss of chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>. Zinc did not affect coral colouration in general, although reflection intensity increased markedly at 100 \u00b5g L<jats:sup>\u20131</jats:sup>, most likely due to a loss of chlorophyll <jats:italic>a</jats:italic>. Our results show that potentially toxic metals such as zinc, found in commercial sea salts and supplements, can have detrimental effects on corals.
